{"type":"assistant","message":{"model":"claude-haiku-4-5-20251001","id":"msg_018qhwHt19eKDxH3MHxqqzoF","type":"message","role":"assistant","content":[{"type":"thinking","thinking":"Let me think about this more carefully. The problem statement says: \"Files that no longer have errors still show the old errors until the user manually opens each file and makes an edit.\"\n\nThis suggests:\n1. File has errors on branch A\n2. User switches to branch B where the file has no errors\n3. The old errors from branch A still show in the Problems panel\n4. Only after editing the file do the diagnostics clear\n\nSo the issue is that the diagnostics collection isn't being cleared when the file content changes significantly.\n\nLooking at the `onDidChangeTextDocument` handler, it calls `requestDiagnostic()` which adds the file to `pendingDiagnostics` and triggers a diagnostic refresh. This should work...\n\nUnless... the issue is that when a file is reloaded from disk by VS Code (when the user chooses \"Reload\" after seeing \"File has changed on disk\"), it might not fire `onDidChangeTextDocument` with the full content change.\n\nOR, the issue might be that for files that aren't open in the editor when the git branch switches, they won't get diagnostics refreshed at all.\n\nLet me search for how the file reload is handled and what events fire.\n\nActually, I think the real solution is simpler. Looking at the file watcher code in typescriptServiceClient.ts, when files change on disk, the client sends watch events to the server. But these watch events don't trigger a diagnostics refresh in the client.\n\nThe fix should be:\n1. When we receive file change notifications (either from `onDidChangeTextDocument` or from file watchers)\n2. We should explicitly clear the diagnostics for those files\n3. Then request new diagnostics\n\nThe key insight is that we might be receiving TWO change notifications:\n1. One from `onDidChangeTextDocument` (if the file is open)\n2. One from file watchers (for all files)\n\nBut the file watcher change might not trigger a UI diagnostics refresh. So we should:\n1. Listen for file system changes more broadly\n\n\n2. Clear stale diagnostics when files are modified on disk\n3.
